Central Bank National Treasury Organization Changes Department to Bureau 112

Hu Mengjia, General Manager of the Bank of Communications, Appointed as Manager

To Be Officially Established Once Preparations Are Complete

The National Treasury Department of the Business Bureau of the Central Bank is being expanded into a bureau, with Hu Mengjia appointed as the manager. The takeover took place the day before yesterday. It will be officially established once preparations are complete. Details are as follows:

Changing the Department to a Bureau: The Central Bank's organization is divided into three bureaus: Remittance, Business, and Issuance. The Business Bureau has a National Treasury Department, headed by Li Tisheng, responsible for the National Treasury's receipts and disbursements, such as tax collection, bond issuance, principal and interest payments, and receipts and remittances for various institutions. Recognizing the heavy workload of the National Treasury Department, a decision was made at a meeting to request the Ministry of Finance to approve the expansion of the organization, changing the department to a bureau, and appointing Hu Mengjia, General Manager of the Bank of Communications, as the Manager of the National Treasury Bureau.

Takeover and Preparations: After Hu Mengjia was appointed as the Manager of the National Treasury Bureau, his position as General Manager of the Bank of Communications was taken over by Tang Shoumin. Mr. Hu went to the National Treasury Department at 9:00 AM the day before yesterday to take over from Department Head Li Tisheng. Preparations began immediately, and the National Treasury Bureau will be officially established once preparations are complete. During the preparation period, the National Treasury will continue to handle receipts and disbursements as usual.

Municipal Government to Convene Various Groups Today to Discuss Improving Fundraising Methods 113

Unifying the Organization in Accordance with Central Government Orders to Show Great Faith

The Municipal Government of this city, in accordance with Executive Yuan Order No. 1384, stated in brief: "Following the order of the National Government, and approved by the Secretariat of the Central Executive Committee, an investigation regarding the collection of donations, both cash and in-kind, used to support and comfort the Volunteer Army and front-line soldiers, or to provide disaster relief to the affected population, the intention is commendable. However, the fundraising methods must adhere to the following principles: (1) Contributing a portion of the spirit or material resources of a group of people to the masses, in order to arouse the sympathy of the majority and obtain their surplus materials; (2) Using the efforts and credibility of an organized minority to arouse the sympathy and excitement of an unorganized populace, and to receive their voluntary contributions of spirit and material resources, along with four resolution methods from the 61st Standing Committee Meeting of the Central Executive Committee (detailed below), in order to avoid the occurrence of abuses." After receiving the order, the Municipal Government convened various groups in this city last Saturday for a discussion at the Municipal Government conference room, with the aim of improving existing fundraising organizations in accordance with the Central Government's orders. Considerable decisions were made as a result. A decision has been made to continue convening various groups this afternoon to discuss this matter, so that work can begin immediately. The four resolution methods from the 61st Standing Committee Meeting of the Central Party Headquarters are recorded below: (1) All national social and cultural organizations, schools, and other organizations that collect donations to support the Volunteer Army, comfort front-line soldiers, contribute to military spending, or provide relief to disaster areas, etc., must contribute their intellectual achievements (such as theatrical performances, recreational gatherings, exhibitions, etc.) to the masses, and arouse their sympathy in order to obtain their donations, or use the efforts and credibility of a formal organization to arouse public sympathy and collect donations of cash or in-kind. The adoption of these methods must be approved by the local party and government authorities. The collection and management of funds must be jointly participated in by personnel outside the organization in order to demonstrate great faith. (2) The collection of the aforementioned donations by national trade associations must be managed by a jointly organized committee. This should be initiated and established by the local party and government authorities to establish the organization, so that the public can easily recognize it and feel sympathy. The collection and management of funds must be jointly participated in by a number of members of the organization, and the amount must be made public in order to demonstrate great faith. (3) The collection of donations for the same item must be organized by the party and government authorities of each province and city into a central agency to oversee its completion and show unity. The aforementioned groups or organizations serve as sub-fundraising agencies, and their establishment is based on the principle of meeting needs without duplication. (4) The local government has the authority to strictly ban anything that does not conform to the above methods.

Sun Ke, President of the Legislative Yuan, accompanied by Fu Bingchang, Ma Chaojun, and secretaries, returned to Nanjing by the 11:30 PM night train last night. Gao Jiyi, Hu Ruoyu, Wang Shuchang, and other former subordinates of Zhang Xueliang came to Shanghai to see Zhang off before he went abroad. They are scheduled to return north by the Beijing-Shanghai express train at 9:20 AM this morning.

Brief Biography of the New SMC Director, Franklin 115

The nine new directors of the Shanghai Municipal Council (SMC) will take office after the Western annual meeting on the 20th of this month, as reported in this newspaper. We now present the following brief biography of Mr. Franklin, the new American director. He graduated from the liberal arts department of a university in Michigan, USA, in 1913. Seeking further advancement, he entered law school and obtained a law degree in another year. At that time, he was only twenty-two years old. On June 1, 1917, he served as Deputy Director of the Legal Group of the U.S. Consul's Office in Honolulu. On November 4, 1918, he served as a First Lieutenant of Infantry in the Headquarters of the Honolulu Defense Command. On June 13, 1919, President Wilson specially appointed him as a First Class Consul in the Honolulu Consul's Office. His political achievements continued to be outstanding. After completing his term, he came to Shanghai at the end of 1921. Various legal groups there prepared letters of introduction for him. The Chinese Chamber of Commerce even prepared a letter of introduction to the General Chamber of Commerce and other legal groups in this city. He immediately began practicing law. Within a few years, he became well-known in all circles and admired by both Chinese and foreigners. Since the recovery of the Public Concession, he has handled cases for the British and American consular offices and has gained the trust of merchants from those countries. Companies such as Electricity, Telephone, Mobil, Socony, Texaco, Asiatic Petroleum, Pro益, and all American-owned banks in Shanghai have hired him as their legal counsel. Because his cases were numerous and he was overwhelmed, he telegraphed a renowned American lawyer, Harrington, to come to Shanghai as his assistant. A number of East China University law graduates are permanently stationed at the office to handle cases in the Special Zone and inland areas. Now that he has been appointed to the new position in the SMC, he will surely use his strengths to seek the common welfare of Chinese and foreign citizens.

Two Ships Collide at the Mouth of the Yangtze River Yesterday Morning 116

Both the Zhengzhou and the British Ship Sustain Minor Damage

The Zhengzhou, a ship belonging to the United Shipping Company at the Wangjia Wharf in Nanshi, arrived in Shanghai yesterday from Haizhou, fully loaded with passengers and cargo. At 5:30 AM yesterday morning, when it entered the mouth of the Wusong River, the "S.S. Parracombe" (transliterated), managed by a British company, was coming from Hong Kong. The ship was steaming full speed ahead. When passing near the first lighthouse on the Shiceng shoal at the mouth of the Wusong River, the Zhengzhou was overtaken. The British ship attempted to pass the Zhengzhou, so its speed was very fast. At that time, the two ships were traveling side by side, but because the tide was very strong, there was a risk of collision. So they sounded their horns to avoid danger, and the bows of the two ships turned away from each other. Unexpectedly, the sterns were too close, so it was difficult to avoid contact, resulting in a collision. The iron plate next to the deck on the port side of the stern of the Zhengzhou was damaged for more than thirty feet. After arriving in Shanghai, the incident was reported to the company for negotiations. It is said that a piece of iron plate on the starboard side of the stern of the British ship was also dented.

It is now planned to hold it next week, and celebrities will be invited to give speeches. Once the date is set, they will be notified. Anyone who served during the European War and is willing to participate in this association can contact Mr. Wei Guangcheng at the Shanghai YMCA, 201 Sichuan Road, or Mr. Gu Xingqing at the AIG Company, 17 The Bund.

The City Will Increase Police Force Next Year 118

| The Municipal Public Security Bureau Has Not Yet Received Official Instructions |

In view of the increasing population density in the urban area and the insufficient police force in each district, the Municipal Government has decided to increase the police force to maintain public order. Severely Beaten by the Kidnappers

Released in Shanghai After Recovering

Zhao Min, a surveyor from the Triangular Survey Team of the Provincial Land Bureau, from Beiping, was dispatched to Jiading last month to survey the terrain. Later, he took sick leave to come to Shanghai for medical treatment and stayed in a certain hotel. Around the 20th of last month, he took money to the New World Company on Yingda Road to shop when he was suddenly kidnapped by a number of bandits and taken to a bandit den. Although he has escaped kidnapping and regained his freedom, he has no travel expenses. Yesterday, he borrowed three silver dollars from a fellow villager on Route Lafayette in the French Concession and took the Beijing-Shanghai express train yesterday afternoon to return to the Provincial Bureau.

Sacrifices of Workers Under Machines 120

| The Number of Deaths is as High as 138 People |

Because there is no mandatory reporting method for factory accidents, it is difficult to know the exact number. According to the court inspection reports and hospital reports obtained by the Public Concession Police Department, in the past six years, 138 people have died in factory accidents, and 119 people have been injured. This also shows the general situation. In addition to major accidents such as explosions and fires, there were also 24 deaths and 4 injuries due to carelessness among machines. Among the deaths, the most were caused by rotating belts, with more than ten people. Either their bodies or clothes were caught in the belts, resulting in death, or they were hit by objects when moving the belts, or people were injured when the belts broke. To prevent this danger, the best method is to add nets to the rotating parts of the belt pulleys as much as possible. Special care must be taken when approaching these parts. Also, when the belts are not in use, they should be racked up, and special poles should be used to place the belts on the pulleys. In modern methods, machines should be divided into parts and become a unified system, so that when repairs are needed, the parts can be temporarily stopped or slowed down. There were also seven deaths due to electric shock in the reports. In addition to accidents caused by broken wires, the rest were due to ignorance. The laws of Western countries require that the metal parts of electric lights be covered, and that the metal parts of all movable machines that may be electrified must be equipped with three-way wires to avoid danger. In addition, five people died from falling due to the lack of railings in elevators. Two people died from broken planing wheels. A rolling machine in a dyeing factory injured two people. A mixing machine in a bakery killed one person. Two people died and one person was injured from accidentally falling into boiling water tanks or oil tanks. Recently, in a weaving factory, a shuttle flew out and injured the eye of a female worker, who has been sent to Guangren Hospital for treatment. The factory law promulgated by the Chinese government stipulates that all deaths or serious injuries in factories must be reported. In the future, accidents can be recorded, and the accidents in one place can be used as a reference for another place.

First Aid Medicine for Front-Line Soldiers 125

The war in North China is becoming increasingly fierce, and the number of wounded soldiers on the front line is very large. However, due to road blockages and transportation difficulties, they are often unable to return to the rear for treatment, and excessive bleeding easily leads to death. Although there is a first-aid medicine called Yunnan Baiyao, it is too expensive and difficult to purchase. Now, Fei Zibin, a tenth-generation physician of the Menghe School of Medicine, has taken pity on this and, based on his accumulated experience and personal insights, invented a first-aid, hemostatic, and pain-relieving medicine. He has successively handed it over to General Zhu Qinglan for transportation to the front line in large quantities, intending to benefit the soldiers and fulfill his national duty. This medicine has incredible efficacy and is even better than Baiyao, but it is cheaper and easier to popularize. For all kinds of gunshot wounds, shrapnel wounds, and knife and sword wounds, if applied to the affected area, it will immediately stop bleeding, relieve pain, and turn danger into safety. Therefore, Xu Shiying, Zhang Xingyan, and others have all given strong praise. Renowned novelist Zhang Henshui also wrote the four characters "Warriors Worry-Free" to promote it. At this time of national crisis, when the two armies are bleeding, it is deeply hoped that kind people and charitable organizations in the country will purchase this magical medicine in large quantities to save the loyal and brave soldiers on the front line. Mr. Fei has poetry and books in his belly and is indifferent to profit. He invented the magical medicine with the aim of helping people and will never use this to make a profit.

New World Company Organizes Charity Society for Employees 126

Pioneering Charitable Undertakings Among Merchants

Creating Many Benefits for the Proletariat

Nearly 1,000 employees of the New World Department Store on Nanjing Road, recently, the company's management and senior employees, in view of the hardship of social life, for the sake of the happiness of the majority of lower-level employees, specially initiated the organization of an employee charity society. The company specially donated a basic fund of 5,000 yuan. Membership is limited to the company's employees. The method of ordinary life insurance is imitated, but the membership fee collected is very small. Lower- and middle-level employees only collect 1 to 2 dimes per month. Those who unfortunately die during their employment period will receive a one-time subsidy of 300 yuan for funeral expenses. If there are family members, they will be given another 200 yuan in alimony, for a total of 500 yuan, so that the families of working-class people who unfortunately die have a line of support for their lives. This is the first charitable organization in a commercial organization.

Chaozhou Fellow Association Sends a Telegram Urging Unanimous Support for Opposition to Soybean Cake Donation 127

The Chaozhou Fellow Association in Shanghai telegraphed the Shantou Municipal Party Headquarters and county-level party branches, and county, city, and township associations, as well as Chaozhou fellow countrymen abroad, saying, "We received repeated telegrams from Shantou merchants that the Shantou Taili Company first deceived the consuls, and then violated the orders, taking advantage of its power to detain dozens of ships carrying domestic soybean cakes from Shanghai, Yingkou, Andong, Hankou, and other places to Shantou, and forcibly ordered them to pay donations. An investigation revealed that the company previously concealed its application to the provincial government to start the Shantou soybean cake donation. Because merchants believed that this exorbitant donation hindered the people's livelihood, they requested permission to cancel it. The company falsely claimed that soybean cakes were imported goods and should be taxed. After the merchants argued that soybean cakes were produced in our country, they secretly asked the financial and educational commissioners to issue a clear order exempting them from taxation. The company then falsely claimed that soybean cakes produced in various places in the three northeastern provinces should be treated as enemy goods, like Dalian in the leased territory, and should be subject to enemy taxation. They did not know that although Yingkou, Andong, and other places had fallen to the enemy, our country was still resisting and had not ceded them to the enemy. How could they be treated as enemy goods by their own people? Even if they were enemy goods, they should have been clearly banned from transport in advance. Why did they detain the soybean cakes at the time of urgent need for spring plowing? Furthermore, how could enemy goods be resolved by paying a heavy donation? Even the customs still taxes them as domestic products. Soybean cake is a domestic agricultural product and should not be subject to heavy donations at all. Now that the situation has become chaotic, the beginning of the disaster can be traced back to the tax farming contractors mismanaging the government. In addition to requesting the provincial consuls to quickly order the release of the detained soybean cakes and to abolish the Taili Company, and to ensure that tax collection is no longer contracted out in the future to eliminate abuses, we urgently request that you uphold the purpose of protecting agriculture and commerce, and help our homeland, and unanimously support and strive to maintain agricultural time and alleviate suffering. We are extremely anxious. The Chaozhou Fellow Association in Shanghai bows.

The pig dealers of Yuanshunyuan, Dachangyuan, Zhaolong, and other pig companies within the Shiliupu of South Shanghai previously rented land in the Xuejiabang of Nanshi to build fresh pig stockyards. Dispute over Breach of Contract for Chartering a Ship Between Two Coal Companies 131

Heng'an Chengji Steamship Company, because the Mainland Yuchang and two coal companies, Wang Xie Hengchuang, violated the ship chartering contract, hired lawyer Cai Rudong and filed a lawsuit in the First Special District Local Court, requesting that the defendant be ordered to pay off the outstanding rent of more than 14,100 yuan. The defendant also hired lawyer Yang Linzhi to submit a statement in defense. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Shen Hong held a court hearing to summon the parties. Lawyer Yang first made a statement on the issue of the subject of the lawsuit, saying that Xie Hengchuang was only the manager of Yuchang, while the manager of the Mainland was Lin Mengchui. Yuchang and the Mainland were actually two organizations and not one entity. The plaintiff said that the company was founded by Xie, and Xie could not admit this. Now Lin Mengchui has also arrived in court on behalf of the Mainland to respond to the lawsuit, so please review this point first, etc. Lawyer Cai immediately said that everyone outside knew that the two companies were opened by Xie Hengchuang. If he denies it, he must provide proof of capital. Empty words are not credible. Lawyer Cai then continued to state the plaintiff's intention to sue, generally saying that the plaintiff and the defendant signed a ship chartering contract on the 3rd day of the 20th year of the Republic of China, chartering the Yunlong steamship to the defendant for a period of one year, with a monthly rent of 8,500 yuan. According to the custom of the shipping industry, after the ship is chartered, it must be declared to the customs to transfer the management rights to the charterer, so the ship was transferred to Yuchang at that time. As of February 9th of last year, the defendant owed rent of 10,238.88 yuan. Although a promissory note issued by Yuchang was received, it was not honored when it was due. The rent of 8,500 yuan for one month from February 10th to March 9th was also not paid by the defendant. In addition, there was a wireless electricity fee of 275.68 yuan paid on behalf of the defendant. After deducting the ship turned over, the coal stored in the ship, the ton tax paid, and the 1,000 tons of coal received from the defendant, valued at 1,200 taels of silver, and a deposit of 800 yuan, the defendant still owed the plaintiff a net rent of 14,113.94 yuan. The defendant claimed to be responsible for the rent only until January 3rd, because he requested to terminate the lease on that date, but the plaintiff did not agree. Lawyer Linzhi then stood up to reply, saying that in addition to the undisputed points, there were two points of contention: (1) The defendant terminated the ship chartering contract on February 3rd and was not responsible for the rent from February 4th. According to the contract, although the one-year term should be from March 9th of last year, the Mainland Coal Company repeatedly sent letters to the plaintiff from February 1st of last year, stating that due to the outbreak of the Anti-Japanese War in Shanghai, the ships could not travel. According to Article 31 of the contract, the ship should not be allowed to sail to the war zone, and the contract should be cancelled, and the location of the ship was informed for receiving. Although the plaintiff replied that he would not agree to terminate the contract, the defendant had actually stopped commanding the ship from February 4th. It was the plaintiff's fault for not receiving it, etc., and cited the lawsuit caused by the Yuan'an Steamship Company and the China and Foreign Steamship Company also terminating the ship chartering contract due to the January 28th Incident as an example. He then continued to state the reasons for his second point of contention, saying that the plaintiff only allowed the rent during the repair period to be deducted as a result of the ship's accident in Qingdao. However, the defendant believed that it should be from December 13th of the year before the accident to the completion of the repair. The ship encountered danger in Qingdao on December 13th and returned to Shanghai on the 23rd. It was put into the dock for repairs the next day until January of last year before it was returned to the defendant for use. Therefore, not only should the rent during the repair period be deducted, but also the rent during the accident period should not be borne by the defendant. According to Article 9 of the contract, if an accident occurs, the charterer may stop paying the rent. All expenses after the accident were listed by Yuchang's Qingdao branch and sent to the plaintiff. In the future, the plaintiff can claim compensation from the insurance company based on the bill. The defendant does not claim to join this case now. For the sake of fairness, the defendant is still willing to compromise on the rent during the accident period. In addition to the 6 days from the 13th to the 18th, which should be fully deducted, from the 19th, the ship set sail from Qingdao to Shanghai and arrived on the 23rd. During these five days, the ship was sailing, and only a small amount of cargo was loaded, so the daily rent should be deducted by half to show fairness. The contract stipulates that if the rent is calculated on a daily basis, then each month should be counted as 30 days. The amount of rent listed in the plaintiff's statement from January 19th to February 9th counts January as 31 days. According to the contract, the defendant should enjoy this day's benefit, so it is specially stated, etc. Judge Shen believed that this case still needed investigation, so he ordered a change of date for further interrogation.

A Construction Worker Fell from a High Building and Died Tragically 134

| His Skull Was Shattered and His Flesh Was Mangled |

The copper building of Qiu Tianbao at No. 7 Zhonghua Road, Xiaodongmen, had old water pipes placed around the roof. The manager of the building, Ying Xiansan, notified the Yushenghongji Manufacturing Factory on Wuchang Road, Zhabei, to hire several construction workers to remove the water pipes and replace them with new galvanized iron water pipes. The factory then sent construction workers Xue Xunquan and Zhang Tao from Pudong to replace them yesterday morning around 9 a.m. After Xue and the others arrived at the building, they stepped onto the roof. Because there were reinforced concrete railings around the top, and the water pipes were installed under the railings, Xue climbed to the outside of the railings, holding the railings with one hand and straightening the other hand to remove the old water pipes below. He was about to replace the new pipes when he did not expect that the vertical file in the railings, although made of cement, was not connected to the railings, but was nailed to the railings with iron nails after being cast. Therefore, the construction was extremely unstable and could not bear the weight, so it broke immediately, and Xue also fell from the third floor, falling to the road. His head and skull were shattered, his flesh was mangled, and the joints of his limbs were also broken. He screamed tragically and fainted from the pain. Zhang Tao and the others then sent him to Shanghai Hospital for treatment. However, due to the severity of his injuries, the rescue was ineffective, and he died in the afternoon. Afterwards, Zhang Tao rushed to Pudong to inform the family of the deceased to come south to prepare a coffin for burial.

The Efficacy of Oil-Saving Devices Oil-saving devices are installed in automobiles, airplanes, and gasoline boats to replace gasoline with diesel, which can save money and increase speed. The inventor, Mr. Bai Er, has spent several years working hard to gradually improve his research results. Now it has finally been completed. A 65-horsepower car with an oil-saving device was tested from Shanghai to Hangzhou in three hours and nine minutes, and from Hangzhou to Ningbo in five hours and twenty-seven minutes, totaling 365 miles. The oil only costs 7.55 yuan, while using gasoline would cost about 50 yuan. The results are very good. This oil-saving device can be installed on any type of car or airplane, and it has the following characteristics: (A) Reduces gasoline and repair costs by about 80%; (B) Increases horsepower and eliminates carbon deposits; (C) Extends mileage by about two or three times; (D) No black smoke; (E) No problem starting the car in extremely cold weather; (F) No need to clean the large fuel injector; (G) Not easy to catch fire. The manufacturer of the device is located at No. 36 Beikai Road. All are welcome to visit. The Deli Ship Brand Cigar Arrives in Shanghai The Honolulu Cigar Factory, founded by a wealthy Chinese-American merchant, produces Deli Ship Brand Flat-Head Cigars, which are very popular among overseas Chinese. These cigars have now arrived in Shanghai in large quantities. They are managed by the Bansheng Guang Company at No. 579 Tianfu Lane, Laobazi Road. All major companies and tobacco shops sell them. Not only is the taste mellow, but also the price is cheap, which is unmatched by any cigar, and the decoration is also very beautiful.

Central Bank Inspection Report 141

157th Time

The 157th inspection report of the Central Bank's issuance reserve stated: According to Article 15 of the Central Bank Regulations, the Association is responsible for inspecting the reserve for the issuance of convertible banknotes by the Bank. The 157th inspection was held at the Issuance Bureau of the Bank on April 10, 1933. The results of the inspection are hereby announced as follows: (A) Total amount of convertible banknotes issued: 44,432,919 yuan in silver standard banknotes, and 4,220,970 yuan in subsidiary currency banknotes. The total amount of the reserve for convertible banknotes was 44,432,9289 yuan, including cash reserves of 36,770,289 yuan in silver dollars. The cash reserve included 31,200,045 yuan stored in the Bank's issuance vault, 3,763,789 yuan stored in branches in various ports, and 1,803,455 yuan stored in peer institutions. The guarantee reserve was equivalent to 7,559,000 yuan in silver dollars. (B) Total amount of customs gold convertible banknotes issued: 417,269.40 yuan in customs gold. The total amount of the reserve for customs gold convertible banknotes was 417,269.40 yuan in customs gold. The reserve included 7,004 taels and 69 cents of gold bullion, equivalent to 417,269.40 yuan in customs gold at the fixed price of 5957. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank's Convertible Banknote Regulations, the cash reserve is 60% and the guarantee reserve is 40%. The inspection results showed that the cash reserve exceeded 60% and the guarantee reserve was less than 40%, which was in line with the regulations. This is hereby reported. April 10, 1933. Chairman of the Board of Supervisors of the Central Bank, Li Fuxun. Supervisors: Wang Jingli, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jilong.

Medical Community 142

Li Shaoguang Establishes an Extra-Curricular Clinic The more civilized the world is, the more complex the diseases become, especially functional diseases are the most common. Such as memory loss, insomnia, stuttering, cheek color, neurasthenia, pressure mania, etc. Since drugs are difficult to attack, they must rely on mental therapy. Moreover, these symptoms do not seem to interfere with the occupation on the surface. Therefore, most people in the middle class and students who suffer from this do not pay attention to it, and they do not have time and money to seek treatment from ordinary doctors. It is recently heard that mental therapist Li Shaoguang, in view of this, has stepped up his work and established an extra-curricular clinic. The time is from 6 p.m. to 9 p.m., and the medical fee has been reduced to two yuan, which can be occupied by those who do not need medicine, to benefit the sick. This is also a unique move in the medical community. Dr. Li's clinic is located at No. 656 Weihaiwei Road (west of Moore Ming Road). The No. 19 public bus can go directly. Telephone number 30065.

Dr. Tang Jiazhen's Treatment Dr. Tang Jiazhen, with profound academic background and deep understanding, is one of the most famous in the Western medical community in our country. He helped the United States for many years and obtained a doctorate degree. After returning to China, he worked in the Peking Union Medical College Hospital for more than ten years. He set up a clinic in Shanghai at No. 3, Lane 281, Jing'an Temple Road. A few days ago, Cheng Zezhou, the inspector general of the political department of the French Patrol Room, and Xia Qifeng, the former secretary of the International League of Nations, both suffered from serious illnesses. After Dr. Tang's diagnosis, they immediately turned the danger into safety, and the disease suddenly disappeared in a few days.

Cide Association Distributes Hemoptysis and Smoking Cessation Tested Prescriptions The China Buddhist Youth Cide Association at No. 113 Baoshan Road, Zhabei, has printed and distributed tested prescriptions for seven consumptions, five injuries, hemoptysis, and gun smoking cessation. There are more than 100 letters from all over the country every day, which shows that there are so many people in our country who suffer from hemoptysis and are addicted to black books. The association is for poor rural areas and poor people who cannot afford to see a doctor, and those who have been addicted to black books and do not have a proven prescription to quit. It has specially reprinted 20,000 copies to spread widely. If you suffer from the above two diseases, you can ask for them in this station without paying a cent. For foreign stations, you must attach a one-cent stamp.

*Two Court Daily Suspends Publication* The Shanghai First Special District Local Court previously believed that the location of the disclosure office was relatively narrow. For the convenience of litigants, it, together with the Second Branch of the Jiangsu Higher Court, issued the *Two Court Daily* starting on March 10, and had posted a notice in the case. Now, because the court's disclosure office has been repaired and expanded, its location is sufficient for application, and because the daily has not been widely sold since its publication, it has not been able to thoroughly implement the original purpose of facilitating litigants. It has been changed to stop publication starting yesterday. In the future, all court announcements, in addition to the usual postings, will still be sent to newspapers for publication, it is said.

Reader Consultant

A Collection of Letters Discussing the Question: "Can We Go Back to the Countryside?" 146

(4) A letter from Mr. Liu Simin of this port (2) Three discussions on "Can we go back to the countryside?"

Yesterday, I read Mr. You's reply to my letter, and hurriedly wrote an article to discuss with Mr. You. Due to space constraints, I will temporarily end here. Now I will raise a few more points for Mr. You and other readers and editors to learn from: (1) The political issue of the "New Utopia." Mr. You first fell into contradiction on this issue. He said that "the new utopia is a village with convenient transportation, scientific production, education, emphasis on hygiene, beauty and purity," which is naturally indifferent to the world, as if to say "Dig a well and drink, cultivate the land and eat, what does the emperor's power have to do with me?" However, Mr. You also said: "We need urban patriots and people of virtue to go to the countryside to lead farmers to transform and build, and to relieve suffering," which is problematic. We want to ask: The so-called suffering of farmers is naturally heavy taxes and miscellaneous taxes. How do you lead farmers to relieve them? The so-called suffering of farmers is of course the exploitation of usury. How do you lead farmers to relieve them? Farmers want to grow grain, but warlords and bureaucrats force them to grow opium poppies. How do you lead farmers to relieve the suffering of this cultivation? Those who cultivate have no land. How do you lead farmers to demand the cashing of the check for "those who cultivate have their land?" Local tyrants, evil gentry, warlords and bureaucrats oppress farmers. How do you lead farmers to relieve their suffering? If in the countryside, some people (naturally the majority) have nothing to eat, and some people's food is "piled up like a mountain," how do you lead farmers to transform and build? The warlords fight each other and want to force farmers to supply food and pay military expenses. How do you lead farmers to relieve this kind of suffering? In the countryside, poor people oppose rich farmers. Which side are you on? Suppose your utopia is in Tongzhou, and the Japanese Marines landed ashore. Naturally you don't fight, naturally you want to avoid it, because our farmers are too "ignorant," as you said, how can your new utopia survive? Hang the sun flag? Otherwise, move to another place, and you can't create such a "beautiful and pure village" for a while, what should you do? Suppose your "new utopia" is in Ganzhou or Fuzhou (southern Jiangxi, western Jiangxi, with beautiful mountains and rivers and convenient transportation, which is most suitable for the construction of Mr. You's new utopia), and the Communist army comes and hangs a red flag at the entrance of your utopia, what do you do? When the National Army comes, they say you are colluding with the bandits, what do you do? A model village in France in the middle of the eighteenth century and a great sacrificer in Belgium could not solve this problem. Their utopias are just a kind of monastery-like operation in capitalist society, using a passive way to maintain capitalist society. What does it have to do with the entire rural economy? Mr. You! We must ask you for a clear answer to these questions. (2) The political issue of "rural education." Suppose Mr. You's "new utopia" is successful and rural education is perfectly realized, then I ask: What do you teach? Mr. You is an agricultural student, so of course it is seed improvement, arable land improvement, sowing improvement, fertilization improvement, mechanization, and electrification. Farmers must have considerable knowledge of general education to reach this point. Young farmers therefore aroused their own awareness. They demanded reform of land relations, demanded the abolition of heavy taxes and miscellaneous taxes, and expressed resistance to local tyrants, evil gentry, corrupt officials, and even united farmers to resist Japan. This kind of movement is inevitable. Then, how do you lead them when you are in the situation? Isn't this kind of education "coughing up tuberculosis?" A friend of mine used to run rural education very successfully, and the children of farmers were all energetic, but he also attracted the attention of the authorities. As a result, the school was disbanded and several students were shot (some said more than a dozen, which are naturally the so-called rioters). He, the old gentleman, ran away. Another friend of mine ran some rural schools near Shanghai, which are said to be very successful. Once I met him, I wished him success, and at the same time I mourned his failure. Because if his rural education is really successful, the children of farmers will definitely not be those docile lambs, and they will definitely not fail to conflict with local gentry and officials, and the result will only be failure. (3) The issue of resisting Japan and "rural education." Now some scholar-officials, in this "sinful" situation of losing the land of four provinces, know that the first condition for real resistance is to let the people rise up themselves and implement national armed mobilization. In this way, the revolutionary national war has expanded, and the power of the people has naturally expanded with it. This is naturally inconvenient. As a result, it can only be submerged under various forms of "long-term resistance," "preparing for resistance," "education to save the country," "learning to defend the country," "economic severance," and "if the enemy comes to attack, we will resolutely resist." Among these various forms, the most powerful one is "education to save the country." Their reason is that workers cannot rise up to resist because they are too uneducated; farmers have even less hope because they are too "ignorant" and too "uneducated." How can this kind of talk not be high-sounding, but what is hidden under this talk! On the one hand, it is to cover up their crimes of losing land and fleeing without fighting, or fighting without strength, or fleeing from this battle to that battle, in order to preserve their bodies and wives. On the other hand, it is to ease the enthusiasm of the mass national war and the anti-imperialist war. As for the real education of the working masses, it cannot be received in any European and American schools, and it cannot be taught by any university professors and students studying in the East and West! As for farmers, it is naturally the same. They may not know a word, but they can deeply feel their own sufferings. Although they cannot chant poems, they all know that local tyrants, evil gentry, and corrupt officials are their enemies. Although they will not say what doctrine or what nation, they are a great force to resist imperialism and overthrow autocracy. The British Magna Carta movement was completed in this way, and the French Revolution went through this way. Mr. You! Do you want to talk about farmer education? Then there is no better education than the French Revolution, and no better education than the Russian Revolution. And this great lesson full of historical significance is the inevitable result of the convergence of various educations of struggle carried out under the slogan of opposing heavy taxes and miscellaneous taxes, reducing rent and grain, opposing corrupt officials, opposing warlord wars, and anti-imperialist wars. Mr. You! I dare say that you have never learned this kind of education in your university lectures and agricultural field experiment reports, definitely not! (4) Who is "honest and without deception." In my previous letter, I refuted Mr. You's words. Yes, I recognized that "most of the upper-class elements are greedy for power and wealth, and the shop assistants and workers are still honest and without deception" (this is borrowing Mr. You's words, and I agree with it very much, although my words are not exactly the same as Mr. You's words). Mr. You said "I am arbitrary" and defended himself: "You must know that there is good and evil, wisdom and foolishness everywhere, and you must never use poverty and wealth as the standard." In fact, this is the fact. I am not saying that there are no one or two good people, honest and without deception, among the scholar-officials. (This kind of ingredient also needs to be discounted), but the vast majority are greedy and snobbish; I am not saying that there are no a few bad people among the shop assistants and workers, but the vast majority are honest and without deception. Moreover, saying that the rich and upper-class elements are not good is not my new invention. Didn't the ancients say "those who eat meat are vulgar?" Didn't they say "full of brains and fat bellies?" Didn't they say "in a high-minded family, ghosts peep into their rooms?" Didn't they say "high sorghum and embroidered articles" have no good children? As for Mr. You's letter of the 8th defending: "I said that the villagers are relatively honest," which is different from the previous letter; the previous letter said: "The villagers are honest, and there is no deception by people in the city," which is a "universal affirmative" logical proposition, and there is absolutely no comparative meaning. Even if you admit that you are saying "comparatively," it also opposes the entire farmers and the entire "city" (should be said "city"). We have already said how the people in the city are above; now let's talk about farmers, middle peasants, poor peasants in the countryside, and vagrant poor peasants in the countryside. Our so-called local tyrants and evil gentry in China are close to the city and have close relationships with commercial capital, industrial capital, and banking capital, and they also have to use fraud. It is not that their parents gave birth to them and they would be fraudulent, but their social relations make them have to be fraudulent. Is this not the fact? Mr. You has been running back to China for more than ten years and has walked through many rural areas. Did he walk with his eyes closed? The rogues in the rural market cheat and take wealth, and cannibalize the poor farmers everywhere. Has Mr. You never seen or heard of them? My maternal family is a farmer, and I can say that I grew up half in the countryside. I know this better and more realistically than you. Finally, I would also like to ask Mr. You to open his eyes and turn around (this is naturally my "fantasy") and face the majority of workers and shop assistants in the city and the majority of farmers, especially the poor peasants, in the countryside. I also want to tell you that those who run from the city to the countryside, at least in Mr. You's mind, the "literate and able to write" friends, do not have the qualifications of "leaders." Their eyes only see landlords and rich farmers. They serve the landlords and rich farmers, and will never stand on the interests of the farmers and poor people to "lead" them. As for the "Mr. Liu," there has never been the word "pessimism" in the dictionary, nor has there been the three words "turn back," please rest assured, but I am very ashamed! Ideas cannot be changed, because I am unwilling to be a high-class Chinese! Also, I read the opinions of Mr. Shi Yu and Mr. Zhang Mei on this issue in the past two days, and many places can supplement the shortcomings of this article. The drama "Mad Current" staged in the cinema recently depicts the development of urban industry, overpopulation, and everyone has no way out. These are all facts, but its conclusion is to teach everyone to go to the countryside. Mr. You's opinion is completely consistent with the main conclusion of this play, which is by no means accidental. What you don't know is that the fundamental reason for the bankruptcy of the countryside is the development of capitalism and the warlord wars, heavy taxes and miscellaneous taxes, etc.; after the countryside is bankrupt, the land is increasingly concentrated, and the rural population is increasingly relatively surplus. Everyone is rushing to the city. There is no way out in the city, but everyone wants to (naturally our "idealists" are thinking) advocate returning to the countryside. They are unwilling to think about the inevitable fate of the future of capitalism, and they dare not think about it, and naturally they dare not make further solutions. Then, there is only turning back! I have more to say, so I will add a few words to ask the readers what they think?

Correction: There are several places in yesterday's Reader Consultant that should be corrected: (1) "Then I realized that Mr. You is a 'pro-Japanese...' agricultural expert!" The sentence "We discuss things and reasons, it is useless to carry the resume on our backs, we have to see what you are showing" is missing below. (2) "Which generation of rich farmers are they 'dear classmates'?" should be changed to "Which class of farmers do they belong to?" (3) The word "commercial" in "As for China's agricultural economy, in the capital and commodities of imperialism and the commercial capital of this country" should be deleted. Communication procedures (1) State full name, age, gender, native place, occupation, detailed address, (2) Attach sufficient return postage stamps, (3) Affix communication stamps in the upper corner of this column. The facts stated in the letter must be simple and clear. The handwriting must be clear. All those who do not attach sufficient return postage stamps and do not state the detailed address will not be replied to, except for those that can be published in this column.

Education News 147

Important News

The Ministry of Education Orders Compliance with Four Regulations on Teachers of Primary and Secondary Schools and Vocational Schools 148

List Special Precautions for Implementation

- Principals must be full-time from June 1 -

(Nanjing, 11th) The Ministry of Education issued a notice to all departments and bureaus, stating that the Ministry has formulated four regulations on primary schools, middle schools, normal schools, and vocational schools. The management, funding, staffing, curriculum, moral education, equipment, academic achievement, academic year, semester, holidays, fee collection, employment of teachers and staff, and school administration of all types of schools have been detailed. In the future, all primary schools, middle schools, normal schools, and vocational schools in all localities must comply with and handle them in accordance with the regulations. The educational administrative organs of each province and city should refer to the local situation to formulate separate regulations and titles, which should be investigated and stipulated separately by the departments. In addition, for all types of existing schools in various localities that need to change their settings and revise their official titles, and for all school principals who still have concurrent positions, they should appoint full-time principals from June 1 this year, and make separate plans and orders to send them. The items that should be paid special attention to when implementing these four regulations in each province and city are listed separately. They should be handled and reported for approval before July this year.

Children of all municipal and private primary school teachers in Hangzhou are admitted to school free of charge 151

The municipal government ordered all schools to comply

The Hangzhou Municipal Government believes that the remuneration of primary school teachers is meager, and during this period of high living standards, most of their children are unable to afford tuition. Municipal primary school teachers have petitioned the municipal government several times, requesting that the children of primary school teachers be admitted to school free of charge, which has been approved by the municipal government. It is now known that the treatment of private primary school teachers in this city is even lower than that of municipal schools. Therefore, Ke Xiaojiao teachers have requested the same reduction and exemption of tuition fees for the children of private primary school teachers, citing the example. After discussion by the Municipal Education Committee, it was decided that the request was true and should be approved to show equal treatment, and the municipal government ordered all primary schools to comply. All children of municipal and private primary school teachers will be admitted to school free of charge.

A group of thirteen people led by Defei

Active Preparations for the City's Secondary School Joint Sports Meet 165

To be Held at the China Athletic Field for Three Days Starting April 27th

Municipal Middle Schools and Approved Private Middle Schools Must Participate

1. The registration deadline is from now until the 20th.

2. Separate participation methods will be determined for secondary physical education schools.

The Shanghai Education Bureau yesterday issued an instruction to the municipal private secondary schools, stating: "In order to promote physical education in all secondary schools in the city, this Bureau has decided to hold the second session of the city's secondary school joint sports meet for three days, from April 27th to April 29th. The regulations have been established and announced. All participating schools should acknowledge the exercise instruction materials, competition guidelines, athlete selection guidelines, and various registration forms for this session of the sports meet. The methods for secondary physical education schools to participate in track and field events have been separately specified according to the regulations. They should be printed and distributed to each school for compliance. Schools should determine the sports items, select athletes, and fill out the registration forms within the specified time limit, and properly submit them to this Bureau for allocation. In addition to separate orders, please find enclosed one copy of the exercise instruction material, one copy of the competition guidelines, one copy of the athlete selection guidelines, seven types of registration forms (one of each), and one copy of the methods for secondary physical education schools to participate in track and field events (this method is only issued to secondary physical education schools)."

Guidelines for Secondary Schools to Select Athletes 166

(1) Eligibility: All male and female students from municipal and private secondary schools in the city that have been approved to be established must participate in the competition. Public secondary schools in the city may also request to participate. (2) Unit: Athletes participate in the competition with the school as a unit. (3) Registration: Athletes from each school participate in the competition and register with the competition division of the organizing committee of the meeting, from April 10th to April 20th. Late registrations will not be accepted. After registration, athletes may not change or add items. (4) Expenses: All miscellaneous expenses required by athletes from each school must be borne by themselves. (5) Competition Rules: The competition rules of this meeting will be based on the competition rules of the Chinese National Sports Federation as a principle.

Competition Guidelines 167

(1) Male and female athletes are divided into Group A and Group B. The grouping criteria are as follows:

Male (Group A): Weighing 115 pounds or more, height 63 inches or more. Anyone meeting either of these criteria will be considered in Group A. (Group B): Those who do not meet the Group A criteria are placed in Group B.

Female (Group A): Weighing 100 pounds or more. (Group B): Weighing less than 100 pounds.

(2) Before participating in various sports competitions, male and female Group B athletes must re-weigh themselves, and male Group B athletes must also re-measure their height.

(3) If there are too many participants in each sports item and it is impossible to compete at once, preliminary rounds, semi-finals, etc. should be held before the finals.

(4) There must be at least six athletes in the finals. If this is not possible in reality, this rule does not apply.

(5) At least two people from each group should be selected in the preliminary and semi-final rounds.

(6) All athletes must make the designated number (consistent with the order on the roster) into two identical and clear symbols, one placed on the chest and one on the back.

(7) Athletes who have given up the right to compete may not rejoin the competition.

(8) Athletes who engage in unethical behavior on the field will have their competition qualifications immediately revoked.

(9) If a track athlete deliberately pushes or runs obliquely to obstruct the progress of others, their qualification will be revoked, regardless of whether it occurs in the preliminary, semi-final, or final round.

(10) Athletes may not use equipment or other powerful stimulants during competition to enhance their movements in order to win.

(11) If an athlete has any protests, they should submit a written appeal to the adjudication committee for review and decision within one hour of the incident.

(12) The protest letter should be signed and sealed by the physical education teacher and the administrative person in charge of the athlete's school.

(13) Once the adjudication committee has decided on the protest, no further protests may be made.

(14) The athletes' uniforms will be made by the schools themselves and must be clean and elegant.

(15) For each competition, the organizer will draw lots to arrange the order of each competitor.

(16) For each field event, competitors should try jumps and throws in the order determined by the organizer.

(17) Field event competitors who are also participating in track events may be allowed to try jumps and throws out of order, with the permission of the field event referee.

(18) The starting position or running route of track athletes will be determined by drawing lots.

(19) If the scores of each competition are the same, those with the same score will have another competition, try jump or throw, raise or lower the height, until a winner is determined.

Methods for Private Secondary Physical Education Schools to Participate in Track and Field Events 168

(1) These methods are formulated in accordance with the provisions of Article 12 of the Regulations of the Second Shanghai Municipal Secondary School Joint Sports Meet.

(2) Track and field events are divided into male and female sections. The items are as follows:

(1) Male: (1) Field Events: High Jump, Long Jump, Shot Put, Pole Vault, Discus Throw, Javelin Throw. (2) Track Events: 100 meters, 200 meters, 400 meters, 800 meters, 1500 meters, 110-meter hurdles, 800-meter relay race, 1600-meter relay race. (2) Female: (1) Field Events: High Jump, Long Jump, Shot Put, Javelin Throw. (2) Track Events: 50 meters, 100 meters, 200 meters, 400-meter relay race.

(3) Male and female track and field events are not divided into groups. Field events are held in conjunction with Group A of ordinary middle schools, and track events are held separately.

(4) Number of participating sports events. Up to four athletes can be sent by each school for each group of track and field events.

(5) Individual championships and team total score winners are not set up for male and female track and field events. Prizes will be given separately.

(6) Four people will be selected for each sports event. Points will be counted using the 5-3-2-1 method. Attached are the methods for private secondary physical education schools to participate in group exercises. Items: 1. General Assembly Exercise. Each school should participate with half of the total number of students. 2. Group Exercises, such as Chinese martial arts walking exercises, flexibility exercises, games, and fitness dances. Each school has a maximum of two sections. (2) Certificates of Merit: Those with excellent performance in group exercises will be given certificates of merit.

General Assembly Exercise Teaching Materials 169

Section 1: Limb Exercises

(1) Left foot steps out to the side, both arms raised horizontally to the sides. (2) Raise heels, both arms raised upward to the sides, clap hands above the head.

(3) Return to the position of (1). (4) Left foot and both arms return to original position. (5678) Repeat the same action with the left foot. Do it for a total of 32 beats. Students call out.

Section 2: Chest-Raising Exercise

(1) Both arms raised forward. (2) Both arms bent in front of the chest, hands clenched into fists. (The upper and lower arms are level with the shoulders, the backs of the hands are facing outwards, pull open forcefully towards the side and rear, while raising the chest. (3) Return to the position of (1). (4) Both arms return to the original position. (567) 8 Same as above. Do it for a total of 32 beats. Students do not call out.

Section 3: Abdominal Exercise

(1) Jump with legs open, both arms bent to the sides. (2) Lean the upper body forward while extending both arms forward (hanging down). (3) Return to the position of (1). (4) Restore to original position. (5678) Perform as described above, up to 32 beats.

Section 4: Turning Exercise

Preparation: Legs open, clench fists, elbows bent flat at the waist, making a hugging fist gesture, upper arms vertical.

(1) Upper body turns to the left while punching out with the left fist (arm level). (2) Upper body returns to the center, right fist retracts. (3) Upper body turns to the right while punching out with the left fist to the right. (4) Upper body returns to the center, left fist retracts. (5678) Same as above, do it for a total of 32 beats until the end, return to standing upright on the last beat.

Section 5: Waist Exercise

(1) Hands on hips, left foot in left lunge. (2) Upper body leans to the left. (3) Upper body returns to straight. (4) Left foot retracts, hands lowered. (5) Hands on hips, right foot in right lunge. (6) Upper body leans to the right. (7) Upper body returns to straight. (8) Right foot retracts. Do it for a total of 32 beats until the end.

Section 6: Fast Action Exercise

(1) Open jump while raising both arms horizontally to the sides. (2) Return to original position. Do it for a total of 32 beats until the end.

Section 7: Breathing Exercise

(1) (2) Raise arms upward from the front, inhale. (3) (4) Lower arms from the sides, exhale. (5678) Same as above, do it for a total of sixteen beats until the end.

Spring and Autumn

Are You Drunk? 182

— Zhan Lu

After the repeal of Prohibition in the United States, I heard that their former Undersecretary of State, Mr. Kessel, gave a speech in Philadelphia, interpreting the Stimson Doctrine, which is known throughout the world, of not recognizing "Manchukuo" in a new light. He believed that this doctrine did not eliminate the possibility that the United States might recognize "Manchukuo," because when the doctrine was initially announced, it did not state that the United States would never recognize "Manchukuo," and so on.

According to Mr. Kessel's reversal, nothing in the world cannot be reversed; because many negative words often do not include the phrase "never." For example, when sentencing a criminal, saying that his crime is unpardonable; if you were to reverse and distort it, you could say: "Unpardonable" does not mean "unpardonable forever"; unpardonable today does not mean it cannot be pardoned tomorrow; unpardonable now does not mean it cannot be pardoned in the blink of an eye. Also, if the words "No Urinating" are written on a plastered wall, you can urinate against the plastered wall. If someone questions you, you can say: "There is no word 'never' on it," which shows that when it was written, people were not allowed to urinate, but now that time has passed, there is a possibility that people are allowed to urinate."

In fact, intending to cancel a previous statement means that even if there is the phrase "never," it is useless; in the Qing Dynasty, a major punishment for officials was called "never to be employed," which seemed that there would never be a day of employment; but the person who was punished only needed to be good at scheming and lobbying, then, the first step would be to request the government to revoke the phrase "never," and the second step would be to become an official again in a grand manner.

Mr. Kessel, could it be that you drank a few more glasses of beer after Prohibition was lifted, which led you to say this drunken talk? You drank American beer and were only temporarily intoxicated, and you will have a clear day soon; if you drank Solar Beer, then it would be terrible! It would be terrible!

Long Live Qin Shi Huang! 183

— Zhang Zhihen

"Collected all the weapons in the world, gathered them in Xianyang, melted them down to make bells and bell stands, and twelve bronze statues, each weighing a thousand stones, placed in the palace." When we read these sentences in the Records of the Grand Historian, Biography of Qin Shi Huang, we understand the Emperor's intentions at that time. Qin Shi Huang unified the world by force, and he was afraid that some people would not accept him, revolt against him, and overthrow his throne of myriad generations of emperors, so he restricted weapons among the people.

Although Qin Shi Huang has been dead for two or three thousand years, his body must have long turned into dust; but his doctrine and spirit are new for all time. Don't you believe it? Recently, there has been an example, let me tell you:

"The British disarmament draft only stipulates that China has 100 airplanes." Although China's land is not large, it is not small either. What is the use of 100 airplanes in national defense? However, the modern world, abandoning Qin Shi Huang, only allows you to have 100 airplanes, dare you not obey? If you make more demands, you must be careful that the modern Qin Shi Huangs will suspect you of having ulterior motives, suspect you of expanding your armaments, wanting to turn over, wanting to make things difficult for them, wanting to overthrow their throne of world hegemony. (Note: There is more than one modern Qin Shi Huang, it is said that there are five, called the Five Great Hegemons.)

The following paragraph was in a certain magazine: "There are between 3,500 and 5,000 commercial airplanes in the United States...and the number is increasing rapidly." Oh dear! Commercial airplanes already have such an alarming number, and the military airplanes are conceivable. Moreover, commercial airplanes can be transformed into military ones.

Someone asked me: "Comparing the numbers 100 and 3,500, is the area of the United States 35 to 50 times larger than that of our country?" I said: "Idiot! There is another reason in this. The Qin Palace may as well put the twelve bronze statues, but we common people are not allowed to hide even one iron nail in our homes. It is already 'imperial grace abounds'."

The spirit of Qin Shi Huang is immortal! Long live Qin Shi Huang!

Unemployment and Love 184

— Zheng Yimei

We Chinese people are bound by thousands of years of ethics and education, so love between men and women is always shy and coy. Except for behind the crystal curtains and beside the trellis, they are never willing to show off affectionate and tender expressions in front of people. Europeans and Americans are more liberated than we are in everything. In public, men and women can hold hands, kiss, hug, and dance without anyone being surprised. Moreover, they have considerable research on love. Love experts have written hundreds and thousands of books, such as "What Men Must Know" and "What Women Must Read," which are read by every household and regarded as golden rules. Men go out to work in the office before 9:00 am and return home after 4:00 pm. If they don't see each other for a day, they will be very affectionate and talk and laugh at this time. Women who are good at being graceful will play a love song after dinner and sing along in a melodious voice, giving their husbands a very pleasant spiritual comfort after being tired all day. Even if they suffer some stimulation or have some depression in their hearts outside, it will disappear invisibly at this time. However, in recent years, the golden country | America | has also felt the tide of depression, and there is a lot of overproduction and unemployment. Those unemployed men, bored and depressed, stay at home all day long. Women feel that their husbands staying at home all day not only does not increase love, but also has the possibility of causing cracks, because affection is difficult to maintain, and the materials for talking and laughing are easily exhausted. Moreover, when they are bored, their moods must be extremely bad. When their moods are bad, they feel that everything is annoying, so the two sides can easily quarrel. Instead of letting love break down at this point, it is better to find a way to maintain it as soon as possible. Therefore, the women's associations in the United States have discussed this issue in detail. As a result, a sacred rule has been set: All unemployed men are not allowed to spend their time at home all day. They still have to go out before 9:00 am and can only come back after 4:00 pm. Therefore, most of those unemployed men hide in small coffee shops in the countryside all day long, singing songs to vent their sorrow. Sometimes they bring a few pieces of coarse bread and run to the mountains and waterside, dazed and silly; performing their art of madness, it's really pitiful!

This news was read to me by my friend Hong Lang from a Western newspaper report, and I wrote it down to share with the Chinese people.

Northeast Fourth Company Commander 185

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Four: The Emotional Situation Reopens, the Teahouse Tilts, and Feelings Accumulate, the End of the Year is Difficult to Pass, and the Pawnshop Sounds of Lament

He saw the old girl from afar, and his heart was full of hope, and he was no longer angry, so when he walked back to his own door, he held the brim of his hat and nodded slightly. For some unknown reason, such an ordinary nod from Ji Zhi made him feel so happy, as if he had gained something from the sky, many times more joyful. For seven or eight days, no matter what he did, he was unhappy, and this was happiness. The next day, Ji Zhi met Gui Zhi head-on on the way home. Gui Zhi was not carrying anything, and did not seem to be buying anything. Moreover, it was almost at the end of the street, and there was no need to come to this place to buy things. He saw that she had a tattered scarf around her neck, and her hands were in her pockets, huddled into a ball. Ji Zhi blocked her face-to-face and said: "Old girl, it's so cold, where are you going?" Gui Zhi replied casually with a very unhappy expression: "Buying something." Ji Zhi smiled and bowed slightly and said: "Old girl, are you still angry?" The old girl smiled faintly and said: "Second Master, how can we bear to say that? What kind of people are we? How dare we be angry with Second Master?" Ji Zhi sighed and said: "It's hard to say, you have to forgive me a little. I'm eating my brother's food now, how can I disobey my brother's orders?" A new milk tea shop has opened at the end of the street. They are from Beijing, and they don't know the people on this street very well. Let's go and have something to eat and talk about it. The street is very cold, and you don't put on any clothes. You came out of the house, be careful of catching a cold." Gui Zhi was originally walking face-to-face, and she could not help but turn around and walk after speaking, and suddenly replied to Ji Zhi: "I'm not cold! I'm not going!" Ji Zhi was met with such a harsh rebuff, what else could he say? He put his hands in the pockets of his overcoat, lowered his head, and walked behind Gui Zhi. Gui Zhi walked twenty or thirty steps ahead and then looked back at him. If they were going home, they should turn at the intersection of a diagonal street, but Gui Zhi did not turn, and kept going straight ahead, which was exactly where Ji Zhi said that a new milk tea shop had opened at the end of the street. Four Hundred and Twenty Thousand 186

— Yongzi

After ten years of study, I earned a colorful, yet useless, graduation diploma. The diploma sits on the shelf, but somehow, business has come along. Thirty-one days in a long month, thirty days in a short month, a salary of forty yuan, a wife, children, high heels, milk powder, the nineteen-column abacus can't make ends meet. Crying to heaven is no use, so the nineteen-column abacus has a stroke of genius and finds a way to make money. Pick up a writing brush, dash off a long article, seriously submit it to the newspaper's editorial office. One day, two days, three days, damn it, the position is taken by the great writer of special contributions. What to do? Ancestral virtue saves me, after ten or eight days, the tile turns over, the editor finds my work in the corner of the drawer, and the printer typesets it without a single error. □ yuan □ jiao □ fen □ li can be included in the budget. But, alas, "a little is better than nothing" is one saying, and "a drop in the bucket" is another. What to do?

"First prize, four hundred and twenty thousand." Haha, fortune has favored me, and I've stumbled into a life of ease. Slowly, the lottery hasn't been drawn yet. No, I'm afraid not to buy it, I spent ten shiny silver dollars, so at least there's a one in one hundred and ten thousand chance of hope. Farting and blowing on fire, perhaps there is such a coincidence in the world. I found a jiao (1/10 of a yuan) walking yesterday, luck is coming, and if I add nine yuan and nine jiao, tighten my belt, save money, and buy a ticket, heaven will not disappoint those who work hard. One, two, three, four, five, six, all six numbers are correct. Piles of colorful, diploma-like banknotes are carried home. This is something to be happy about.

Buying lottery tickets is gambling and can foster a gambling mentality. I can't accept that label. Fortunately, this is charitable in nature and shouldn't be equated with gambling. Whoever wants to get rich is doing good. If you're missing teeth and have a runny nose, you get two benefits at once. There are so many poor guys like me in the world, working as clerks, doing literary begging, never dreaming of earning eighteen thousand in a lifetime. Only by enthusiastically doing good and buying champagne can you catch small fish and then big fish. Fellow comrades who want to get rich, this is a once-in-a-lifetime opportunity.

Wood Crafts

Thoughts After Visiting the Industrial and Railway Exhibition 187

— Chuan Yi Zhi

The National Chiao Tung University held an Industrial and Railway Exhibition. All the newspapers in Shanghai had detailed reports, causing a national sensation and a time of great prosperity. During the Qingming Festival in the old calendar, I also took the opportunity of a holiday to visit. The exhibits were dazzling and beautiful. Unfortunately, I'm not an industrial expert. For various machine structures and their principles, even after detailed instructions by internal staff, I still couldn't fully understand them. However, I will briefly mention my thoughts as follows:

(1) Domestic Automobiles: Promoting domestic products should start from a broad perspective. In recent years, many business giants in China have been ambitious about domestic goods. However, their own cars and the transportation vehicles needed for the circulation of domestic goods are all purchased from abroad, which doesn't seem to be a fundamental solution. Only the Shenyang Mortar Factory painstakingly researched and manufactured several trucks, which meant that domestic automobiles could be produced in large quantities from now on and there was no need to rely entirely on foreigners. Unexpectedly, during the September 18th Incident, the factory was destroyed, and all the self-made trucks were looted by the violent Japanese. Only one, which was transported to the National Roads Association for display, is now displayed again at the Industrial and Railway Exhibition. We no longer hear of similar domestic automobiles being produced. Seeing this luckily surviving relic, one can't help but feel sentimental and sigh!

(2) Water Pumps: In recent years, the urban population has been increasing day by day. The only reason is the bankruptcy of the rural economy. Farmers cannot support themselves and have to seek a living in cities. However, the reasons for the bankruptcy of the rural economy are nothing more than floods, droughts, wars, and the lack of improvement of agricultural tools and seeds. I grew up in the countryside and know the situation well. For example, in years of severe drought, in addition to using hand-operated waterwheels to draw a small amount of water for irrigation, one can only pray to heaven for rain. The exhibition has water pumps displayed by the China Iron Factory and the Aurora Iron Factory. It is said that irrigation of fields is a hundred times more efficient than manual water scooping. The one I saw was a four-horsepower water pump, priced at about a hundred yuan. Unfortunately, the person attending it seemed to be a worker, and he vaguely answered how many gallons of water could be absorbed per minute and whether it could absorb water from a low position to a high position over a long distance, so I couldn't fully understand its effectiveness. If it could be as ideal as we imagine, its benefit to drought relief would be significant. I hope those engaged in rural undertakings will pay attention to it, which is also a way to save the rural economy.

(3) Comparison of Highways in Various Provinces: In the exhibition section on national road achievements, there is a comparative chart of highways in various provinces, with red lines indicating completed highways and green lines indicating planned but uncompleted ones. The length of red and green lines is the longest in Guangdong and the shortest in Jiangxi. I think that transportation convenience is directly proportional to cultural development and inversely proportional to rampant bandits. The banditry in Jiangxi has been spreading endlessly, is it because of this? As a Jiangxi native, I can't help but feel ashamed. I still remember that during the January 28th Incident, the enemy reinforcements arrived quickly like divine soldiers, while our reinforcements were transferred from southern Jiangxi, detoured through Zhejiang and Quzhou, and walked for a month before reaching the Shanghai-Hangzhou area. Therefore, I can't help but hope that the authorities will actively complete the national highways to help with foreign affairs. (4) Others: Most of the exhibits at the exhibition are machine industries, such as English typesetting machines, which only require one person to type and can automatically cast the required characters, saving time much more than manual typesetting. In addition, such as electric motors, transformers, and various locomotives, are all great and ingenious. Unfortunately, they are all products of foreign machine factories, and our country is far behind. I hope that the Chinese people will rise up and catch up, so that the saying of saving the country through industry will not become empty talk!
